**[CHAR-10]** E — Enticement *captures and intensifies* affect: 2Pe 2:14 — "insatiable for sin" — sustained enticement produces an affective state of insatiable craving; the appetite deepens through its engagement with the enticement mechanism. Hypocrisy *exploits* affect: the desire for social belonging (affective) is what makes collective hypocrisy attractive (Gal 2:13 — conforming to the group is affectively rewarding). Apostasy *redirects* affect: the covenantal allegiance (affective commitment) is abandoned and redirected.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The condition *captures and misdirects* the affective faculty. Rom 6:12 — sin deploys bodily passions as instruments of its reign — the affective capacity (passions, desires) is captured by the condition and redirected toward its sinful objects. Rom 7:5 — "sinful passions... at work in our members" — the passions are the affective content that the condition activates and deploys. The condition does not eliminate affect but misdirects it: the passions remain operative but serve sin's reign rather than God's.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Sin's enslaving power *captures* the affective faculty. Eph 4:26 — the anger that is not resolved becomes a doorway to sin; the enslaving power uses unchecked affect (sustained anger) as a mechanism of entry. The practice-to-slavery mechanism (Joh 8:34) requires sustained desire-driven practices; the affective desires are what drive the practices that generate the enslavement. The enslaving power thus operates through and deepens the affective captivity: once enslaved, the affective draws toward sin continue and reinforce the slavery.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The record *deepens negative affect* when conscience is engaged: Psa 38:18 — sorrow; Eze 33:10 — despair. But when conscience is suppressed, the record *bypasses affect*: Isa 3:9 — sin proclaimed without shame — the affect of shame is absent despite the record's presence. The record exists independently of the affective state; affect is the conscience's variable response to the record, not a constitutive feature of the record itself.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Forgiveness received *deepens and redirects* the affective faculty. Luk 7:47 — the forgiveness produces love as a deepened affective capacity directed toward God; the previously sinful affective orientations of the woman are redirected by forgiveness toward love. The self-affliction of seeking (Lev 23:27) is not suppressed affect but *directed* affect: sorrow channelled into the seeking posture. Forgiveness received does not eliminate the affective capacity but transforms its direction (from sinful loves toward love of the forgiver).

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The generational pattern *deepens negative affect* over time. Jer 8:14's despair and Isa 64:5's salvific uncertainty are the affective consequences of the "long time in our sins": the prolonged duration of the condition deepens the affective state from acute sinning-recognition toward chronic hopelessness. The question "shall we be saved?" (Isa 64:5) names an affective state of uncertainty about liberation that the long duration of the generational pattern has produced.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — The sinner-identity *produces characteristic negative affects* and *misdirects positive affects*. In the sinner: Isa 33:14 — dread (appropriate but too late); Luk 18:13 — grief (appropriate and productive). In the observer: Pro 23:17 — envy (inappropriate — drawn toward the sinner's apparent prosperity); Psa 26:9 — fear (appropriate — awareness of contagion danger). The sinner-identity does not eliminate the affective faculty but distorts it: it can produce dread without repentance (Isa 33:14 — too late for the VCG-03 sinners) or envy without discernment (Pro 23:17).

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — The guilt-state *activates and deepens negative affect*. Ezr 9:6 — shame activated by guilt-recognition; Gen 4:13 — despair deepened by the punitive-weight dimension. The accumulated guilt progressively deepens the affective burden: 2Ch 33:23 — "Amon incurred guilt more and more" — the progressive guilt-accumulation progressively deepens the affective weight without address. Conversely: Isa 6:7 — "your guilt is taken away" — the removal of guilt is followed by the implicit affective liberation; the removal reverses the affective burden.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — The iniquity-weight *deepens negative affect* when engaged and *bypasses affect* when suppressed. Psa 38:4/40:12 — the recognised weight produces deepening grief, shame, and overwhelm. Hos 12:8 — "I am rich... no iniquity in me" — the suppressed iniquity produces no negative affect; the person feels prosperous confidence despite accumulating crime. The affect is thus a reliable indicator of conscience-engagement: shame and sorrow (Psa 38:18; Ezr 9:6) accompany honest acknowledgment; false confidence (Hos 12:8) accompanies suppression.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Transgression *misdirects* the affective faculty (Pro 17:19 — love directed toward transgression itself) and *deepens negative affect* under accumulation (Lam 1:22 — heart fainting; Eze 33:10 — despair). The primary affective distortion is Pro 17:19's "whoever loves transgression loves strife" — the love-faculty attached to transgression produces both the affective pleasure of wrongdoing and the consequent strife. The remedy produces positive affect: Psa 32:1 — "blessed is the one whose transgression is forgiven" — forgiveness produces blessedness as the opposite affective state to transgression-burden.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Faithlessness *misdirects* affect toward the wrong object (Pro 11:6 — lust capturing the treacherous person's affective faculty) and *produces negative affect* in its victims (Lam 1:2 — bitter weeping) and spiritually-aware witnesses (Ezr 9:4/10:6 — grief and mourning). The lust-as-driver (Pro 11:6) and desire-for-violence (Pro 13:2) show that faithlessness co-opts the affective faculty and redirects it toward objects that betray rather than sustain the covenant. The productive affect: the grief of Ezra (Ezr 9:4/10:6) — the appalled response of a covenant-faithful conscience.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Perversion *inverts* the affective faculty: what should produce shame produces delight (Pro 2:14 — rejoicing in evil) and what should be straightforward produces mourning (Psa 38:6 — bowed down under the weight of sin). The affective inversion is one of perversion's clearest markers: Gal 6:8 — "sows to his own flesh" implies an affective orientation toward fleshly desire that drives the corruption; 2Pe 1:4 — "corruption that is in the world because of sinful desire" — desire as the affective driver of corruption.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Injustice *eliminates* the appropriate shame-affect in the unjust person (Zep 3:5 — "knows no shame") and *provokes* distress-affect in the righteous (Psa 37:1 — fretfulness; Psa 43:1 — urgent appeal). The double affective pattern: the unjust person feels nothing (no shame); the righteous person feels the fretful impact of witnessing injustice going apparently unpunished. The absence of affect in the unjust and its presence in the righteous-witness is CHAR-22's most distinctive affective feature.

---

### T3.4.3

**Question:** What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The pattern reveals that wilful sinning is an *affectively mediated* act of the will: the will does not sin in an affective vacuum but rides available affective currents (fear, anger, contempt) in its sinning direction. This is why the prescriptive deterrents are also affective (fear of God before you, Exo 20:20) — the corrective is not to eliminate affect from the will's operation but to redirect which affect is operative. The characteristic thus sits at the intersection of volition and affect: the will + the wrong affect = sinning; the will + the right affect (fear of God) = deterrence.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The limited affective evidence (post-realisation guilt in Lev 5:5; contrition in Num 22:34) reveals that affect in CHAR-2 is temporally displaced relative to the act: it arises upon realisation rather than during the sinning. This contrasts with CHAR-1 where affect (fear, contempt, anger) may operate during the sinning itself. The temporal displacement of affect in CHAR-2 is a structural feature of inadvertent sinning: the affective moral response is delayed by the same knowledge-gap that made the sin inadvertent.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The affective pattern reveals that genuine confession includes an honest affective acceptance of the moral reality named: shame (Jer 3:25; Dan 9:8), indignation borne (Mic 7:9), and the emotional weight of inherited moral failure (Lam 5:7). These affective dimensions are not produced by confession but are part of the complete confessional act — the conscience names the sin, the will agrees, the mouth speaks, and the affect accepts the appropriate moral weight of what was done. Hollow confession distinguishes itself by skipping this affective acceptance.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The affective pattern reveals that conscience suppression maintains itself partly through *affective reinforcement*: the false peace of Jer 2:35 ("his anger has turned from me") is more comfortable than the fear and shame that accurate moral self-awareness would produce. The characteristic is therefore not only a cognitive and conscience failure but also an affective one — the person is sustained in the suppressed state partly because the suppressed state feels more comfortable than the alternative. This is why Paul specifically targets shame as the corrective affect (1Cor 15:34) — shame is the affective disruption of the false ease.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The affective pattern reveals that refusal to repent is *affectively maintained* as well as volitionally chosen: the dulled moral affect (1Ki 16:31) removes the motivating force of moral revulsion; the affective attachment (2Ki 3:3 — "clung to") adds a positive pull toward the sinful course. Together these affective conditions make turning away emotionally difficult: there is insufficient negative affect to motivate departure and positive affective attachment binding the person to the sinful course. The appropriate corrective affects are fear of God (1Ti 5:20) and revulsion at sin — restoring these is part of what makes turning possible.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The affective pattern reveals that habitual defection is not affectively neutral: it involves the transference of the deepest affective capacity (reverential fear/allegiance — 2Ki 17:7) to wrong objects. The habitual sinner's affect is not absent but misdirected — which is both a diagnosis (the affective faculty is working in the wrong direction) and an indication of what correction requires (the reorientation of the affective allegiance back to God, not merely a behavioural change).

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The affective pattern reveals that contagious sin is not merely behavioural but affectively constitutive: the community's redirected fear/allegiance toward idols (2Ki 17:7; 1Ki 16:13) names an affective transformation that the transmitted sinning has produced. The community is not merely performing sinning actions; they have come to genuinely fear (reverence) false gods. This deep affective transformation is the most enduring consequence of contagious sin: surface behaviour changes more easily than formed affective allegiance. Josiah's structural demolition (2Ki 23:15) can remove the altar; redirecting the affective allegiance from false gods back to the Lord is the deeper task that structural demolition alone cannot accomplish.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — The silence on affect is consistent with the corpus's regnal-narrative literary form: political history is described at the factual level without inner-affective description. The absence of affective vocabulary marks CHAR-8 as the most externally-focused characteristic in the M10 cluster — the corpus does not access the inner affective experience of either the revolting parties or the governing authority.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The affective pattern reveals that sinful speech is *affectively generated and affectively reinforcing*: it arises from the affective register of bitterness, anger, and pride, and it consolidates those states through the act of verbal expression. The prescriptions of Eph 4:31 and Col 3:8 thus address the affective root ("put away bitterness and wrath") alongside the speech-output ("slander... from your mouth") — recognising that renouncing the speech without renouncing the affective root is insufficient. The affective renunciation must accompany the verbal renunciation.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — The affective pattern reveals that enticement is the mechanism most directly and deeply engaged with the affective faculty: the desire/appetite is itself an affective reality, making enticement the characteristic's primary affective mechanism. 2Pe 2:14's "insatiable for sin" shows the endpoint: the affective faculty captured and locked into a self-deepening craving cycle. The other two mechanisms engage affect instrumentally (hypocrisy through social-belonging affect; apostasy through covenantal-allegiance affect) rather than constitutively.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The affective pattern reveals that the universal sin-condition operates partly through the capture of the person's affective motivational system. Sin's reign (Rom 6:12 — reigning through passions) is an affective-level dominion: the person is made to *obey* the passions that sin deploys, suggesting that the affective drive overrides the cognitive-moral will. This explains why the condition's liberation is not merely cognitive (knowing what is right) but must address the affective level: Rom 6:13 — the body must be actively re-presented to God, redirecting the affective system's deployment from sin's instruments to God's instruments.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — The affective pattern reveals that sin's enslaving power has an affective entry-point: Eph 4:26 — sustained anger is the affective gateway through which sin's power can enter; Joh 8:34 — the practices that generate slavery are driven by affective draws toward sinful objects. The enslaving power exploits affect as the mechanism of practice-generation. Eph 4:26's practical instruction ("do not let the sun go down on your anger") addresses the affective entry-point directly, prescribing its closure before sin's enslaving power can use it.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The affective pattern reveals that the divine record does not require affective engagement to exist — the record is objective (the definition: "whether they feel it or not"). Affect is the optional inner-being register of the record when conscience is functional: sorrow (Psa 38:18), despair (Eze 33:10), and hopelessness (Eze 33:10 — "how then can we live?") are the primary negative affects the record produces. The positive resolution of the record (forgiveness and erasure) produces the corresponding positive affect: Psa 32:1 — "blessed is the one whose transgression is forgiven" — blessedness is the positive affective state of having the record addressed.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — The affective pattern reveals that Luk 7:47's love-magnitude-proportional-to-forgiveness-magnitude is the characteristic's defining affective insight: the depth of the affective response (love) is the measure of the depth of the received forgiveness. This principle reveals that the characteristic is not merely a legal transaction (sin-record cancelled) but has a proportional affective consequence: greater forgiveness received produces greater love; lesser forgiveness perceived produces lesser love. The affective faculty is the thermometer of forgiveness received.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The affective pattern reveals that generational sin produces a characteristic affective trajectory: early persistence (Psa 78:17/32 — still sinning without apparent affective weight) → prolonged condition (Isa 64:5 — "a long time") → despair and doom-recognition (Jer 8:14 — "doomed to perish") → salvific uncertainty (Isa 64:5 — "shall we be saved?"). The long duration of the generational condition progressively deepens the negative affect from indifference through despair to fundamental doubt about the possibility of salvation.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — The affective pattern reveals that the sinner-identity produces a distinctive affect spectrum: from the extreme sinner's dread before divine fire (Isa 33:14 — extreme type at judgment) through the self-aware sinner's penitential grief (Luk 18:13 — productive affect) to the observer's envy of the sinner's prosperity (Pro 23:17 — misdirected affect). The productive affective response to the sinner-identity is Luk 18:13's breast-beating grief that issues in the plea for mercy — this is the affect that opens the way to repentance (Luk 15:7 — joy over the sinner who repents).

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — The affective pattern reveals that shame (Ezr 9:6) is the primary affective expression of guilt-recognition (VCG-01/02) while despair/overwhelm (Gen 4:13) is the primary affective expression of guilt-as-punitive-weight (VCG-04). The affective spectrum runs from productive shame (Ezr 9:6 — that leads to acknowledgment before God) through paralysing despair (Gen 4:13 — "greater than I can bear"). The productive affect (shame leading to acknowledgment) enables the guilt-resolution process; the paralyzing affect (despair) precludes it.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — The affective pattern reveals that shame (Ezr 9:6) and sorrow (Psa 38:18) are the productive affective responses to iniquity-recognition — they initiate the confession-to-removal pipeline (Lev 26:40/41 — heart-humiliation → confession → divine response). The unproductive affect is the false prosperity-confidence of the iniquity-denier (Hos 12:8). Between these poles: Psa 40:12's heart-failure is the overwhelm-affect of iniquity accumulation without address — not the productive sorrow that leads to confession but the paralysing despair that it has become too much.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — The affective pattern reveals that the love-of-transgression (Pro 17:19) is the most distinctive affective feature of CHAR-19 — it is the affective dimension in which the person actively enjoys the crossing. This is what distinguishes CHAR-19 from CHAR-2 (unintentional sin — which involves no affective pleasure in transgression): the deliberate boundary-crosser can develop a positive affective orientation toward the transgression itself. The resolution brings blessedness (Psa 32:1) that is the affective opposite of both the transgression's pleasure and its consequent burden.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — The affective pattern reveals two characteristic affect-profiles for CHAR-20. (1) *The faithless person's affect*: lust (Pro 11:6), desire for violence (Pro 13:2) — affects directed toward the betrayal-target; (2) *The covenant-faithful person's affect in response to faithlessness*: Ezra's grief (Ezr 9:4/10:6), Lamentations' bitter weeping (Lam 1:2) — affects expressing the damage faithlessness causes. CHAR-20 is distinctive in generating intense negative affect in the faithful-witness (Ezra's night-mourning without food or water) — the most intense expressed grief-response in M10's studied characteristics for a non-self-directed sin.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — The affective pattern reveals that Pro 2:14's "delight in the perverseness of evil" is the most analytically significant affective finding for CHAR-21: the person has achieved an affective positive-orientation toward what is inverted. This is not neutral wrongdoing but joyful embrace of perversity — the affective faculty has been so thoroughly perverted that evil's distortion is a source of pleasure. This affective-delight-in-perversity distinguishes CHAR-21 from characteristics where wrongdoing is reluctantly pursued or passively sustained.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — The affective pattern reveals that Zep 3:5's shamelessness diagnostic names the affective elimination that constitutes the fully formed unjust character. The unjust person who "drinks injustice like water" (Job 15:16) has eliminated the disgust-affect that should naturally accompany wrongdoing. The righteous observer's fretfulness (Psa 37:1) is itself named as a danger to be resisted — the psalmist's counsel against fretful envy toward wrongdoers shows that the righteous person's affective response to injustice must also be governed.

---

## T3.5 — Creativity

### T3.5.1

**Question:** Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Limited evidence. The closest engagement of the creative/imaginative faculty is in the planning dimension: Neh 6:13 — enemies "hired" Shemaiah and constructed a scenario designed to produce sinning in Nehemiah ("for this purpose he was hired, that I should be afraid and act in this way and sin"). The planning and construction of the trap implicates creative faculty on the temptation-design side. On the sinner's side, Hos 13:2 — "they sin more and more, and make for themselves metal images, idols skillfully made of their silver, all of them the work of craftsmen" — shows that escalating sinning produces increasingly elaborate creative output (skilfully made idols), implicating creative investment in the sinning pattern.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — The 18-verse corpus contains no evidence of creative-faculty engagement in connection with unintentional sinning. The characteristic operates through knowledge-gap and inadvertence, not through imagination or origination. No creative-faculty evidence is present.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(S)*

**[CHAR-3]** S — The corpus contains no evidence of creative-faculty engagement in connection with confession. Confession is retrospective and naming-focused, not imaginative or originating.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(S)*

**[CHAR-4]** S — The corpus contains no evidence of creative-faculty engagement in connection with conscience suppression. The characteristic operates through absence and failure rather than creative origination.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(S)*

**[CHAR-5]** S — The corpus contains no evidence of creative-faculty engagement in connection with refusal to repent. The characteristic operates through will, heart, and inherited pattern rather than through imagination or creative origination.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — The corpus contains no evidence of creative-faculty engagement in connection with habitual defection. The characteristic operates through will-habituation, affective misdirection, and relational-epistemic blindness rather than through imagination or creative origination.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Limited creative-faculty evidence. Jer 32:35 — "they built the high places of Baal in the Valley of the Son of Hinnom" — the building of the high places is an agentive creative act. The creative-constructive faculty is used in the service of the sinning transmission: physical structures are built as vehicles for the sinning practices. The creative capacity (to build, to design worship spaces) is deployed toward sinning structures rather than toward God-oriented worship structures.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Limited creative-faculty evidence. 2Ki 8:20 / 2Ch 21:8 — "set up a king of their own" — the establishment of an alternative governing structure requires creative-constructive agency: the revolting community creates new political institutions (kingship) in place of the broken governing relationship. The political creativity of establishing independent governance is a constructive dimension of the revolt.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Limited creative-faculty evidence. Rev 2:9 — "the slander of those who say that they are Jews and are not" — the false claim requires creative fabrication: the slanderers invent an identity they do not possess. The creative faculty is engaged in the *construction of false claims* — sinful speech in the slander-register may require inventing or elaborating falsehoods about persons or about God.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — The 5-verse corpus does not evidence creative-faculty engagement in connection with enticement, hypocrisy, or apostasy. The mechanisms operate through desire-exploitation, social conformity, and will-departure rather than through creative origination.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(S)*

**[CHAR-11]** S — The 112-verse corpus does not explicitly engage the creative faculty in connection with sin as universal condition. The condition operates through power-domination, debt, passions, and the indwelling force — not through creative origination.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — The 9-verse corpus does not evidence creative-faculty engagement in connection with sin's enslaving power. The characteristic operates through captivity-mechanisms rather than creative origination.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Limited evidence. Pro 24:9 — "the devising of folly is sin" — the cognitive-creative act of scheming folly creates a record entry. The creative faculty in its inverted form (devising folly rather than creating good) is engaged as a sin-generating mechanism that enters the record. Isa 30:1 — "who carry out a plan, but not mine" — the creative plan-making that departs from God's purposes adds sin to sin; the creative faculty deployed against God's will is a record-generating activity.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(S)*

**[CHAR-14]** S — The 34-verse corpus does not explicitly engage the creative faculty in connection with forgiveness sought and received. The characteristic operates through the volitional-seeking, cognitive-recognition, affective-love, and relational-restoration dimensions rather than through creative origination.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-15]** S — The 8-verse corpus does not explicitly engage the creative faculty in connection with generational sin. The characteristic operates through corporate moral identity, volitional rebellion, and memory-failure rather than through creative origination.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(S)*

**[CHAR-16]** S — The 64-verse corpus does not explicitly engage the creative faculty in connection with the sinner-as-moral-character. The characteristic operates through constituted identity, social categorisation, conscience recognition, and affective response rather than through creative origination.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(S)*

**[CHAR-17]** S — The 97-verse corpus does not explicitly engage the creative faculty in connection with guilt as inner-being state. The characteristic operates through conscience, memory, affect, will, and relational-restitution rather than through creative origination.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(S)*

**[CHAR-18]** S — The 162-verse corpus does not explicitly engage the creative faculty in connection with iniquity as accumulated moral crime. The characteristic operates through conscience, memory, will, and relational accountability rather than through creative origination.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(S)*

**[CHAR-19]** S — The 147-verse corpus does not explicitly engage the creative faculty in connection with transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing. The characteristic operates through will, cognition, affect, conscience, and memory rather than through creative origination.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-20]** S — The 101-verse corpus does not explicitly engage the creative faculty in connection with faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin. The characteristic operates through will, spirit, conscience, affect, and covenant-allegiance rather than through creative origination.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes — through the evil-devising dimension. Pro 6:14 — "with perverted heart devises evil" — the devising is a creative-cognitive act; the perverted heart produces plans and schemes; Pro 16:30 — "whoever winks his eyes plans dishonest things" — the planning is a creative-cognitive activity directed toward evil; Isa 32:7 — "he plans wicked schemes to ruin the poor with lying words" — elaborate planning of perverse schemes.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes — through the devising and searching dimensions. Psa 58:2 — "in your hearts you devise wrongs" — devising is a creative-cognitive act; Psa 64:6 — "they search out injustice, saying, 'We have accomplished a diligent search'" — the analytical-creative effort applied to finding opportunities for injustice; Hab 2:12 — "woe to him who builds a town with blood and founds a city on iniquity" — the creative-constructive faculty deployed toward building civic structures on injustice.

---

### T3.5.2

**Question:** Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The evidence from Hos 13:2 suggests that wilful sinning *misdirects* creativity — the creative faculty produces increasingly elaborate substitutes for God (skillfully crafted idols) rather than what it was designed to produce. The creative capacity is not impaired (the idols are skillfully made) but its direction is perverted by the sinning orientation. This is the characteristic's effect on creativity: not suppression but misdirection.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — No evidence. The corpus is silent on creativity in the context of unintentional sinning.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(S)*

**[CHAR-3]** S — No evidence. The corpus is silent on creativity in connection with confession.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(S)*

**[CHAR-4]** S — No evidence. The corpus is silent on creativity in connection with conscience suppression.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(S)*

**[CHAR-5]** S — No evidence. The corpus is silent on creativity in connection with refusal to repent.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — No evidence. The corpus is silent on creativity in connection with habitual defection.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Contagious sin *misdirects* the creative-constructive faculty: Jer 32:35's high places of Baal are creative acts whose product is the vehicle for child sacrifice ("to offer up their sons and daughters to Molech"). The creative capacity to build and design is engaged in constructing the structures that transmit and institutionalise the sinning direction. The creative faculty remains fully operative but is deployed in the service of the contagious sinning pattern rather than in the service of God-directed worship.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Political revolt *channels* the creative-constructive faculty toward political institution-building: 2Ki 8:20 — "set up a king of their own" — the creative capacity to establish governance is exercised in the service of the revolt's positive assertion of independence. The characteristic does not impair creativity but deploys it in the construction of alternative political authority.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Sinful speech *misdirects* the creative faculty toward fabrication and false claim construction. Rev 2:9's false identity claim shows the creative capacity for self-definition being used to produce a false identity that slanders what is genuinely God's (the true community). The creative capacity to speak and define is directed toward false speech rather than true.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — No evidence. The corpus is silent on the creative faculty's engagement with these mechanisms.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(S)*

**[CHAR-11]** S — No direct evidence. The condition's relationship to creativity is not addressed in the corpus. The condition's primary modes (enslaving power, standing debt, passions-capture) are not creative-faculty operations.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — No evidence. The corpus is silent on the creative faculty's engagement.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The record *captures and misdirects* the creative faculty. Pro 24:9 — the devising (creative cognitive act) of folly is itself sin; the creative capacity is deployed toward the wrong object and generates a record entry. Isa 30:1 — the plan-making faculty (creative will) that pursues alliances not of God's Spirit adds to the sin-record. The creative faculty's operation against God produces record entries; it is captured by sinful purpose rather than creative goodness.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(S)*

**[CHAR-14]** S — No direct evidence. The corpus is silent on the creative faculty's engagement with forgiveness sought and received.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-15]** S — No evidence. The corpus is silent on the creative faculty's engagement with generational sin.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(S)*

**[CHAR-16]** S — No direct evidence. The corpus is silent on the creative faculty's engagement with the sinner-identity.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(S)*

**[CHAR-17]** S — No direct evidence. The corpus is silent on the creative faculty's engagement with guilt as inner-being state.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(S)*

**[CHAR-18]** S — No direct evidence. The corpus is silent on the creative faculty's engagement with iniquity as accumulated moral crime.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(S)*

**[CHAR-19]** S — No direct evidence. The corpus is silent on the creative faculty's engagement with transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-20]** S — No direct evidence. The corpus is silent on the creative faculty's engagement with faithlessness.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Perversion *misdirects* the creative faculty toward evil's devising. Pro 6:14 — "continually devises evil" — the creative-cognitive capacity is captured and deployed toward schemes of harm and discord. The "continually" (*kol-hayyôm* — all the time) confirms that the perverted heart's creative capacity is perpetually directed toward evil rather than occasionally. The creative faculty is thus not eliminated by perversion but redirected — the perverted person can be diligently creative in scheming harm.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Injustice *misdirects* the creative faculty toward unjust ends. Psa 58:2's "devise wrongs" and Psa 64:6's "diligent search for injustice" show the creative-analytical capacity engaged toward planning wrong. Hab 2:12's city-building on iniquity shows the constructive faculty deployed toward civic injustice. The creative capacity is not eliminated but redirected from creative right-order building to creative wrong-order building.

---

### T3.5.3

**Question:** What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The limited evidence (Hos 13:2; Neh 6:13) suggests that wilful sinning does not primarily operate through the creative faculty — it is not constitutively a creative act. The creative dimension appears as a secondary effect (elaborated idolatry) rather than the primary mechanism. The characteristic's core is volitional (will choosing the wrong) with creativity as a vehicle for expressing and deepening the sinning pattern over time, not as its origin.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — The silence on creative-faculty engagement is consistent with the characteristic's nature: unintentional sinning is not a creative act. It arises from the absence of knowledge rather than from the active exercise of any faculty. The silence is expected.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(S)*

**[CHAR-3]** S — The silence on creative-faculty engagement is consistent with confession's retrospective naming structure. This prompt is closed.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(S)*

**[CHAR-4]** S — The silence is consistent with conscience suppression's nature as a failure-mode characteristic. This prompt is closed.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(S)*

**[CHAR-5]** S — The silence is consistent with the characteristic's nature as a volitional-dispositional phenomenon. This prompt is closed.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — The silence is consistent with the characteristic's dispositional nature. This prompt is closed.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The creative-faculty pattern reveals that contagious sin captures and deploys the image's creative capacity for structural sinning: the same capacity to build worship structures that was designed for God-directed worship is redirected to construct sinning-transmission vehicles (high places, altars). This is consistent with CHAR-7's broader pattern of image-capacity inversion: authority, creativity, memory — all designed for God-oriented community formation — are captured by the sinning pattern and deployed in its service.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The creative pattern reveals that political revolt is not only destructive (breaking the prior relationship) but constructive: the revolting community creates new political structures as the positive assertion of independence (2Ki 8:20). This constructive dimension distinguishes political revolt from mere non-compliance: revolt builds alternative governance, not merely refuses existing governance.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The creative pattern reveals that sinful speech can deploy the image's creative-speech capacity — the capacity to name, define, and declare — in the direction of false naming, false definition, and false declaration. This is the inversion of the image's designed creative-speech function: the image-bearer is designed to speak truth (including truth about God); sinful speech uses the same creative-speech capacity to speak falsehood (about God and persons).

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — The silence on creativity is consistent with the mechanisms' non-creative character: enticement exploits what exists (desire), hypocrisy performs an existing identity pattern, apostasy departs from an existing commitment. None require or primarily engage creative origination. Noted.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(S)*

**[CHAR-11]** S — The silence on creativity reflects the characteristic's focus on the person's condition before God (sin as structural state, debt, enslaving power) rather than on the person's creative productive capacity. The condition is primarily about what sin has done to the person's inner-being standing, not about what the person creates. Noted.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — The silence on creativity is consistent with the enslaving-power characteristic's focus on captivity (not creation), structural imprisonment (Gal 3:22), and constitutional identity (1Jo 3:8/9). Noted.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The creative pattern reveals that the divine record is not only generated by obvious moral failures but also by the active cognitive-creative deployment of the person's planning and devising capacities toward ends contrary to God (Pro 24:9; Isa 30:1). The record captures what the mind devises and what the will plans, not only what the body does overtly. This confirms the record's comprehensive scope: it is sensitive to inner creative-cognitive movements as well as outer acts.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(S)*

**[CHAR-14]** S — The silence on creativity is consistent with the characteristic's focus on the restoration of the sin-broken relationship rather than on creative origination. Forgiveness restores what sin damaged; it does not primarily operate through the creative faculty. Noted.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-15]** S — The silence on creativity is consistent with the characteristic's focus on inherited corporate moral identity rather than individual creative capacity. Noted.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(S)*

**[CHAR-16]** S — The silence on the creative faculty is consistent with the characteristic's focus on constituted moral identity (who the person is) rather than creative production (what the person makes). The sinner-identity is received or formed, not created. Noted.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(S)*

**[CHAR-17]** S — The silence is consistent with the characteristic's focus on the retrospective (backward-looking) conscience-recognition of past violation rather than the forward-looking creative faculty. Guilt-as-inner-state looks backward at what was done; creativity looks forward toward what might be made. Noted.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(S)*

**[CHAR-18]** S — The silence is consistent with CHAR-18's backward-looking nature: the characteristic is the accumulated record of what has been done rather than the forward-looking creative generation of what might be. Noted.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(S)*

**[CHAR-19]** S — The silence on the creative faculty is consistent with CHAR-19's constitutive volitional nature: the characteristic is defined by the will's act of crossing a given boundary rather than the creative generation of new boundaries or possibilities. Noted.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-20]** S — The silence is consistent with CHAR-20's constitutively relational-covenantal nature: the characteristic is about the disposition within an existing bond, not creative generation of new realities. Noted.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — The creative pattern reveals a significant distinction from CHAR-20 (faithlessness) and CHAR-19 (transgression): CHAR-21 is the only M10 characteristic studied that explicitly evidences engagement of the creative-devising faculty. Pro 6:14's "perverted heart devises evil continually" names the creative capacity as captured by perversion. This confirms CHAR-21 as M10's characteristic of active inner distortion rather than passive failure — the perverted heart is not merely wrong but actively, creatively wrong.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — The creative pattern confirms Psa 58:2's characterisation: injustice is not a passive failure but an active devising — the heart creatively plans wrong before the hands enact it. Psa 64:6's "diligent search" for injustice names the systematic, analytical effort the unjust person invests in finding opportunities. This active-creative wrongdoing dimension distinguishes CHAR-22 from accidental or negligent wrong: the unjust person is a creative agent of planned wrongdoing.

---

## T3.6 — Volition

### T3.6.1

**Question:** Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The volitional faculty is the *primary* faculty engaged by wilful sinning — this is the defining claim of the characteristic. Every verse in the corpus presupposes an active will. Eze 18:4/20 (the soul who sins carries personal accountability — accountability is only coherent for a willing agent). Gen 39:9 (Joseph's refusal is a volitional act: "how then can I do this?"). 1Sa 15:24 (Saul's will capitulates to social pressure: "I obeyed their voice"). The entire VCG-03 deterrence corpus assumes the will can choose not to sin (Exo 20:20, Psa 4:4, Psa 119:11, Eze 3:21). The will is the origin, the executor, and the accountable agent of wilful sinning.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The volitional faculty is engaged in CHAR-2 in a qualified sense. The sinning act itself involves the will — the person did something (Lev 4:2 — "does any one of them"; 1Sa 14:33 — "the people are sinning against the Lord by eating with the blood"). The will executed the act, but without the moral information that would have engaged the will's knowing-refusal capacity. The will is thus present in the sinning (it performed the act) but not in the mode that constitutes wilful sinning (it did not choose against a known prohibition). Balaam (Num 22:34) explicitly offers his will for redirection: "if it is evil in your sight, I will turn back" — the will is now fully informed and ready to act in the opposite direction.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Yes — and the volitional faculty's engagement is the distinguishing criterion between genuine and hollow confession. 1Ch 21:17 — "It is I who have sinned and done great evil. But these sheep, what have they done? Please let your hand, O Lord my God, be against me and against my father's house" — the will claims ownership (I who have sinned), distinguishes its agency from the innocent (the sheep), and redirects the consequence onto itself — volitional engagement at full depth. Luk 15:18/21 — the prodigal's confession involves a volitional movement (arising, going) that enacts the confession as an act of the will, not merely a speech. Deu 1:41 (VCG-03) — the will confesses verbally but then moves autonomously — the volitional engagement is partial.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The volitional faculty is engaged in the active-denial mode. Jer 2:35 — "you say, 'I am innocent'" — the will chooses to make the false claim and maintain it. The will is the faculty through which conscience suppression becomes an active act rather than a passive condition: the will decides to deny what the conscience (however dimly) might register. In the habituated mode (Ecc 8:12 — sinning "a hundred times"), the will is engaged as the faculty that repeatedly chooses sin despite the available moral standard — the will has been habituated to sinning without moral restraint.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The volitional faculty is the *primary* faculty engaged — refusal to repent is constitutively a will-act. The entire corpus is volitional language: "did not depart," "did not turn," "would not obey" (Neh 9:29), "sinning deliberately" (Heb 10:26 — *hekousiōs* = willingly). The will is the faculty that has the capacity to turn and is refusing to exercise it in the direction of turning. The characteristic is impossible without an operative will — the will must be functioning for there to be a refusal; an absent or non-functioning will would be CHAR-4 (Conscience suppression) territory.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The volitional faculty is the *primary* faculty of habitual defection — but in its *dispositional* mode rather than its moment-of-choice mode. 1Sa 2:25 — "they *would not* listen" — the "would not" is an expression of settled volitional direction: the will is disposed against listening; it is not making a fresh choice to refuse but is operating from a habituated refusal-disposition. Hos 10:9 — "there they have *continued*" — the continuation is volitional persistence: the will sustains its sinning orientation without requiring a new decision at each moment. Exo 9:34 — "sinned yet again and *hardened* his heart" — the hardening is a volitional self-formation: the will contributes to its own increasing rigidity.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The volitional faculty is the primary faculty engaged at both ends of the contagious sin structure. In the leader: "walked in the way of Jeroboam" (1Ki 16:26) — the will's personal commitment to the sinning course; "made Israel to sin" (Hiphil causative) — the will's causative exercise of authority toward transmitting the sinning direction. In the community: 2Ki 17:21 — "drove Israel from following the Lord" — the community's will is redirected from God-following to the sinning direction. The volitional engagement is real at both ends: the leader's will causes the transmission; the community's will is reshaped by it.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Yes — the volitional faculty is the primary faculty engaged. Pa.sha is a deliberate wilful act: the decision to break submission and act on that decision is constitutively volitional. 2Ki 1:1 / 3:5 — "Moab rebelled against Israel" — the rebellion is an act of the Moabite community's political will. 2Ki 8:20 / 2Ch 21:8 — "Edom revolted... and set up a king of their own" — both the breaking from and the establishing of new governance are volitional acts. 2Ch 21:10's causal chain shows volition operating at both the ruler level (Jehoram's volitional forsaking of the Lord) and the political level (Edom's and Libnah's volitional revolt).

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Yes. The volitional faculty is engaged at the point of externalisation. Jude 9 — Michael "did not *presume* to pronounce a blasphemous judgment" — the restraint is a volitional act; the will withholds the word. Rev 13:5 — the beast's blasphemous words are a sustained willed production ("it was allowed to exercise authority for forty-two months"). 1Ti 6:4 — the "craving for controversy" is a volitional appetite for the conditions that produce sinful speech. The will either restrains (Jude 9) or enables and sustains (Rev 13:5) sinful speech.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Yes — the volitional faculty is engaged by all three mechanisms, differently in each. (1) *Enticement*: Jam 1:14 — the enticement mechanism draws the will through desire — the will yields to the desire's pull rather than resisting. 2Pe 2:14 — "hearts trained in greed" — the will has been formed to desire and choose greed as its habitual orientation. (2) *Hypocrisy*: Gal 2:13 — "acted hypocritically along with him" — the choice to act alongside in hypocrisy is a volitional adoption of the performed identity. (3) *Apostasy*: Act 21:21 — "forsake Moses" — forsaking is a volitional act of departure from the covenantal commitment.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes — the volitional faculty is the most consistently named inner faculty across the corpus. (1) *The enslaved will*: Rom 7:17/20 — "it is no longer I who do it, but sin that dwells within me" — the will's identity is preserved but its effective control is overridden; (2) *The will's obedience as the master-choice*: Rom 6:16 — "you are slaves of the one whom you obey" — the will's act of obedience determines whose slave the person is; (3) *The will commanded to resist*: Gen 4:7 — "you must rule over it" — the volitional faculty is addressed as the faculty that must exercise governing authority against the sin-force; (4) *The will freed*: Rom 6:18 — "having been set free from sin, have become slaves of righteousness" — liberation changes the will's master-relationship.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Yes — the volitional faculty is the *primary* faculty engaged, by the characteristic's definition. Joh 8:34 — "a slave to sin" — slavery is the condition in which the will cannot freely choose otherwise; the will is the faculty whose freedom the enslaving power eliminates. Gal 3:22 — "the Scripture imprisoned everything under sin, so that the promise by faith in Jesus Christ might be given" — the imprisonment prevents the will from obtaining the promise through human effort; only faith (the will's response to the promise) can receive it. 1Jo 3:9 — "he cannot keep on sinning" — the "cannot" names a constitutional volitional impossibility that the new birth creates as the counter to sin's volitional enslavement.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes — the volitional faculty is engaged at the generation and the departure levels. (1) *Will generating record entries*: Lev 26:18/21/24/28 — "if you will not listen to me" — the wilful refusal is what triggers sevenfold discipline; the will's persistent refusal accumulates the record; (2) *Will departing from the record*: Eze 18:21 — "if a wicked person turns away from all his sins that he has committed" — the volitional turning is what reverses the record's account against the person; Eze 33:14/16 — "if he turns from his sin" — the will's turn is what enables the record's erasure; (3) *Will clinging to the record*: VCG-04 — "he did not depart from the sins of Jeroboam" — the will's persistent clinging perpetuates the institutional legacy.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes — the volitional faculty is the primary faculty of the seeking dimension. Act 2:38 — "repent and be baptized" — repentance is a volitional act; baptism is a volitional submission to the ritual. Exo 32:30 — "I will go up to the Lord" — the volitional first-person declaration of Moses's seeking. Lev 23:27 — the community must afflict themselves (volitional self-directed act) and present offerings (volitional act of bringing). Act 10:43 — "everyone who believes" — believing is the will's trust-commitment to Christ as the forgiver.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Yes — the volitional faculty is centrally engaged as both the sustainer and the potential breaker of the generational pattern. (1) *Sustaining*: Psa 78:17 — "rebelling against the Most High" — the will's active rebellion sustains the inherited sinning pattern; "sinned still more" implies escalating volitional commitment; (2) *Breaking*: 1Ki 8:47 — "if they turn their heart... and repent" — the turning is a volitional reversal; repentance is the will's decision to move in a different direction; Eze 37:23 — "they shall not defile themselves anymore" — the future volitional commitment to non-defilement is the pattern's reversal.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes — at three points. (1) *Consent to enticement*: Pro 1:10 — "if sinners entice you, do not consent" — the will's consent is the gateway through which the sinner-identity can be adopted or deepened; the volitional "do not consent" is the alternative; (2) *Volitional transactionalism*: Luk 6:32/33/34 — sinners love, do good, and lend only within reciprocal relationships — the will operates within a self-interest radius; the sinner's volitional orientation is calculating and return-seeking; (3) *Volitional repentance*: Luk 15:7 — "one sinner who repents" — the repentance is a volitional turning that reverses the sinner-identity's direction.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes — at both the guilt-generating and guilt-addressing levels. (1) *Will generating guilt*: Jer 3:13 — "acknowledge your guilt, that you rebelled against the Lord" — the guilt arose from a wilful act of rebellion; 2Ch 33:23 — "Amon incurred guilt more and more" — the progressive accumulation is a sustained volitional pattern; Hos 10:2 — "their heart is false" — the false-heart-driven choices generate the guilt; (2) *Will addressing guilt*: Lev 5:5 — guilt-realization → "confesses... and will restore" — the will's decision to confess and restore; Lev 6:4 — "realized his guilt and will restore" — the will's initiative in restitution.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes — as both the source and the addressed faculty. (1) *Will as source*: Eze 14:3 — "taken their idols into their hearts" — the will's inner choice to receive idols is the volitional origin of the heart-seated iniquity; Jer 16:12 — "because you have done evil, even more than your fathers" — volitional escalation; Psa 106:43 — "they were rebellious in their purposes" — the will's rebellious orientation generates iniquity; (2) *Will as the required faculty for change*: Lev 26:41 — "if then their uncircumcised heart is humbled" — the will must choose humility as the precondition for iniquity-address; Hos 14:2 — "take with you words and return to the Lord; say to him, 'Take away all iniquity'" — the will's initiating speech-act of return.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — The volitional faculty is the primary faculty of CHAR-19 — the definition names it: "the will that knowingly crosses a boundary." (1) *Will as the agent of transgression*: Isa 1:2 — "they have rebelled against me" — the will's choice of defiance; Eze 2:3 — "nations of rebels who have rebelled against me" — sustained volitional rebellion; Hos 8:1 — "they have transgressed my covenant" — the will's covenant-breaking; (2) *Will as the required faculty for remedy*: Eze 18:30 — "repent and turn from all your transgressions" — the repentance-turn addresses the will; Isa 59:20 — "those who turn from transgression" — the turning is volitional.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — The will is the primary faculty of CHAR-20. (1) *Will as agent of allegiance-transfer*: 1Ch 5:25 — "broke faith with the God of their fathers, and whored after the gods of the peoples" — the will's active transfer of covenant-allegiance; Eze 18:24 — "when a righteous person turns away from his righteousness" — the will's volitional turning; (2) *Will as the subject of spirit-guarding*: Mal 2:15/16 — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and do not be faithless" — the command is to the will to guard the spirit; (3) *Will as the faculty that deepens under pressure*: 2Ch 28:22 — Ahaz's will "became yet more faithless" — the will choosing faithlessness with increasing determination rather than turning.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes. (1) *Will actively embracing perversion*: Pro 2:14 — "who rejoice in doing evil and delight in the perverseness of evil" — the will positively orients toward perversity; Pro 16:30 — "whoever winks his eyes plans... he who purses his lips brings evil to pass" — the will executes the perverse plan; (2) *Will captured by corruption*: 2Pe 2:19 — "slaves of corruption... For whatever overcomes a person, to that he is enslaved" — the will is enslaved by what once it chose; Eph 4:22 — "old self... corrupt through deceitful desires" — the desires override the will's capacity for self-direction.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — The will is the primary governing faculty of CHAR-22. (1) *Will enacting injustice*: Eze 3:20 — "a righteous person turns from his righteousness and commits injustice" — the volitional turn; Psa 58:2 — devising and dealing out violence — the will committing and executing; (2) *Will restraining from injustice*: Eze 18:8 — "withholds his hand from injustice" — the will's active restraint; (3) *Will choosing to cease*: Job 34:32 — "if I have done iniquity, I will do it no more" — the volitional commitment to stop; Eze 33:15 — "walks in the statutes of life, not doing injustice" — the will walking away.

---

### T3.6.2

**Question:** Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with other characteristics, and the constraints under which it operates?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Wilful sinning *expresses* volition (the will is actively choosing) while *deepening constraint on future volition* over time. The escalation evidence (Hos 4:7 — "the more they sinned"; Hos 13:2 — "they sin more and more") shows a progressive narrowing of the will's range: each act of sinning makes subsequent sinning more likely and more compulsive. Neh 13:26 — "foreign women made even him to sin" — implies that sustained exposure progressively undermines the will's capacity to resist. The will that wilfully sins remains technically free (the corpus maintains moral accountability throughout) but its effective range is progressively constrained by habituation.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Unintentional sinning operates through *uninformed volition* — the will acts without the moral information that would enable it to choose rightly. This is not impairment of the will but operation of the will within an information deficit. The remedy sequence (confession → offering → forgiveness) restores the will's alignment: Num 22:34 (Balaam's will, now informed, offers to reverse) shows the will in its corrected mode post-disclosure. The characteristic does not impair volition; it reveals the will's dependence on adequate moral information to operate rightly.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Genuine confession *aligns and deepens* volition: the act of naming sin as sin before God commits the will to a moral position — by confessing "I have sinned," the will agrees with the conscience's verdict and moves toward alignment with God's moral standard. 2Sa 24:10 — "please take away the iniquity of your servant" — the confessing will is oriented toward restoration and away from the sinning direction. Hollow confession (Deu 1:41) shows that verbal confession without volitional alignment does not enable the will — the will remains on its own course.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Conscience suppression *both enables and impairs* volition. It *enables* the will to choose sin without the moral resistance that an active conscience would create — Ecc 8:12 (sinning a hundred times is possible partly because no inner check is operating). It simultaneously *impairs* the will's capacity for right moral choice: a will habituated to sinning without conscience (Tit 3:11 — "warped") progressively loses the inner equipment it needs to choose well.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Refusal to repent *misdirects* volition while keeping it fully operative. The will remains fully functioning — it is making choices, clinging to the sinful course, resisting correction (Neh 9:29 — "would not obey" is an act of will). But the direction of volitional operation is away from God and away from the available turn. Over time, sustained refusal *constrains* volition: Heb 10:26 — "there no longer remains a sacrifice for sins" — the persistent-refusal will progressively forecloses the options available to it (the sacrifice is closed off). The will is not impaired in its operational capacity but progressively constrained in its available options through sustained refusal.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Habitual defection *misdirects and progressively constrains* volition. The will remains operative — the habitual sinner keeps sinning, keeps refusing to listen, keeps directing allegiance elsewhere — but its directional freedom is progressively constrained by the habit it has formed. Exo 9:34's hardening cycle shows this: each iteration of sinning-and-hardening makes the will's sinning direction more natural and the alternative less accessible. The self-reinforcing structure (Hos 8:11 — altars for sinning producing more sinning) shows how habitual defection builds an environment in which the will's sinning direction is the path of least resistance.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Contagious sin *misdirects* the leader's volition (toward causing others to sin) and *shapes* the community's volition (toward the sinning direction). For the leader, the will is fully operative and causatively engaged — there is no impairment, only a wrong direction. For the community, the will is gradually shaped toward the sinning direction through sustained exposure to the leader's transmitted sinning (1Ki 22:52 — three generations; 2Ki 21:11 — Manasseh's sustained idolatry shaping Judah). The community's volitional freedom is not removed but its default orientation is progressively shaped toward the sinning course.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Political revolt *expresses* volition at full capacity: the revolt is a decisive exercise of the revolting community's collective will. The corpus shows no impairment — the volitional capacity is fully engaged in the breaking and the constructive establishment of alternative authority. 2Ki 3:7 — Jehoram's immediate political-military response to Moab's revolt shows the governing authority also exercising full volition in the response. Volition is fully operative on both sides of the revolting relationship.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Sinful speech *misdirects and progressively binds* the will. 1Ti 6:4's craving — the will's appetite for controversy — feeds on the sinful speech it produces: slander generates more craving, and the craving generates more slander. VCG-03's beast-blasphemy shows the endpoint: the will entirely bound to the sinful speech orientation as its constitutive expression (Rev 17:3 — "full of blasphemous names"). The will is not impaired in its operational capacity but is progressively bound to the sinful speech pattern.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Different patterns. (1) *Enticement impairs volition*: Jam 1:14 — the enticement mechanism draws the will through desire before the will has made a deliberate choice; the desire pre-empts deliberate volition. 2Pe 2:18 — "those who are barely escaping" — the barely-escaping person's will is weakened, making the desire-exploitation more effective; enticement targets and exploits volitional weakness. (2) *Hypocrisy misdirects volition*: Gal 2:13 — the will makes a choice (to act alongside) but the choice is driven by social pressure rather than authentic identity. (3) *Apostasy exercises volition*: Act 21:21 — the departure is a volitional act; the will chooses to stand away from the covenantal commitment.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The condition *enslaves and progressively captures* volition. Rom 7:14 — "sold under sin" — the will is in a slave-ownership relationship; its capacity for autonomous choosing has been compromised by the sale. Rom 6:20 — "when you were slaves of sin, you were free in regard to righteousness" — the enslaved will has no freedom toward righteousness; the will's freedom is preserved in one direction (sinning) while closed in the other (righteousness). The condition's enslavement is thus a directional impairment: the will can continue to choose within the sinful domain but cannot freely choose toward God.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Sin's enslaving power *captures and progressively binds* volition. Joh 8:34 — the will of the practice-sinner is progressively captured through the accumulating practices; each practice-act deepens the will's directional captivity toward sin. The will is not eliminated (the person continues to choose and act) but its free direction toward God is foreclosed: Rom 6:1/2 — "continue in sin... live in it" — the enslaved will continues choosing within the sin-domain but cannot exit the domain through its own freedom.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The record *accumulates through volitional persistence* and *is addressed through volitional turning*. The will's sustained choices in one direction deepen the record (Lev 26:18-28 — sevenfold escalation; VCG-04 — kings who did not depart). The will's decisive turn enables the record's erasure (Eze 18:21; 33:14/16). The record thus tracks the will's directional history precisely: VCG-04's "he walked in" and "he did not depart" language is the volitional vocabulary of record accumulation.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Forgiveness received *liberates* volition. Col 2:13 — "dead in your trespasses... made alive" — the death-in-trespasses suppresses volitional freedom (the dead cannot will effectively); the forgiveness that makes alive restores the volitional capacity. Act 2:38 — "you will receive the gift of the Holy Spirit" — the Spirit's indwelling following forgiveness is the source of renewed volitional capacity; the Spirit enables the will's ongoing God-directed freedom that sin had foreclosed.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The generational pattern *captures and progressively deepens* volitional commitment to sinning: Psa 78:17 — "sinned still more" — the volitional momentum is in the direction of increasing sin; the "still more" indicates the will becoming progressively more committed to the inherited direction rather than less. However, 1Ki 8:47 confirms the will retains the capacity to turn (the heart can be turned; repentance is possible), meaning the generational pattern does not eliminate volition but skews its default direction.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — The sinner-identity *constrains and narrows* volition. Luk 6:32/33/34 — the sinners' volitional range extends only to reciprocal relationships; they love those who love them, do good to those who do good, lend to those who will repay. The sinner-identity confines the will to a self-interest radius: the will can operate within that radius (genuine love, real goodness — Luk 6:33 notes sinners genuinely "do the same") but cannot extend beyond it without a deeper transformation. The volitional capacity is not eliminated but limited in its reach.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — The guilt-state *redirects volition* toward remedial action when conscience operates correctly. Lev 6:4 — "realized his guilt and will restore" — the guilt-state produces a volitional impulse toward restitution; Num 5:7 — "he shall confess... and shall make full restitution" — the guilt-recognition is the volitional turning-point. However, the unaddressed guilt-state can *paralyse volition*: Gen 4:13 — "my punishment is greater than I can bear" — Cain's experience implies a volitional paralysis under overwhelming punitive guilt; 2Ch 33:23 — "incurred guilt more and more" — the will persisting in guilt-generating choices despite accumulation shows volition captured by the wrong direction.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — The iniquity *captures and constrains* volition progressively. Pro 5:22 — "the iniquities of the wicked ensnare him, and he is held fast in the cords of his sin" — the accumulated iniquity becomes the cords that bind the will; voluntary choices have produced an involuntary bondage. Eze 18:30 — "lest iniquity be your ruin" — the warning presupposes the will can still turn; before the bondage becomes total, the will retains the capacity to repent. The progression is: free volitional choice of iniquity → accumulation → progressive bondage of will → ruin. The iniquity does not eliminate will immediately but ensnares it progressively.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Transgression *progressively enslaves* the will that committed it. Psa 19:13 — "let them not have dominion over me!" — transgression seeks dominion over the will; Pro 29:6 — "ensnared in his transgression" — the will is trapped by what it chose; Pro 12:13 — "ensnared by the transgression of his lips" — the spoken transgression returns to ensnare the speaker's will. The progression is: free volitional act (the first crossing) → repeated crossings → accumulated ensnaring → dominion over the will. The will that chose transgression is progressively constrained by what it chose until it requires divine liberation.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Faithlessness *progressively captures* the will. Pro 11:6 — "the treacherous are taken captive by their lust" — the faithless will is eventually captured by the very desire that drove it to betray; 2Ch 28:22 — the will that chose faithlessness progressively loses its freedom to turn toward God (each distress-event produced more faithlessness, not less). The will begins as the agent of betrayal (the choice to break faith) and ends as the captive of the betrayal's consequences (lust-captivity). The remedy (Lev 26:40 — "if they confess") requires the will's active engagement in the confession-act.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Perversion *captures and enslaves* the volitional faculty progressively. The initial active-will choice of perversity (Pro 2:14 — delight in perverseness) produces the enslavement of 2Pe 2:19 — "slaves of corruption"; whatever overcomes the person enslaves them. The will that freely chose perversity is progressively incapacitated by what it chose. The remedy (Eph 4:22-24 — "put off... put on") is a volitional act requiring renewal of the spirit of the mind (Eph 4:23 — "renewed in the spirit of your minds").

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Sustained injustice *progressively captures* the will. The initial volitional choice to commit injustice (Eze 3:20 — "turns and commits") develops toward the fixed-character dishonesty of Luk 16:10 — consistent across small and large — where the will's choices are no longer deliberated afresh but flow from the constituted unjust character. The will that could have withheld (Eze 18:8 — "withholds his hand") becomes the will that consistently enacts wrong at every scale. The remedy calls the will back to volitional choice: Job 34:32 — "I will do it no more."

---

### T3.6.3

**Question:** What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The pattern reveals that wilful sinning is a *volitional act with volitional consequences*: the will that sins remains the responsible agent (Eze 18:20 — "the soul who sins alone shall die") but exercises its agency in a direction that progressively constrains future agency. The characteristic is constituted by the will's exercise, but its sustained exercise progressively reshapes the will's default orientation. This is the deepest finding of the T3.6 cluster: sinning is wilful, but sustained wilful sinning is self-undermining of the very volition that produces it.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The volitional pattern reveals that *the will alone is insufficient for moral integrity* — the will requires accurate moral information (knowledge of the commandments, awareness of the morally relevant facts) to operate in alignment with God's standards. Unintentional sinning exposes the gap between the will's capacity and the information the will needs to exercise that capacity rightly. This is a theologically important insight: moral failure does not require a wilfully defiant will; it can occur through an uninformed will operating normally within its creaturely limitations.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The volitional pattern is the key diagnostic of genuine vs hollow confession: the will must agree with and enact what the mouth says. 1Ch 21:17 shows this alignment at full depth — the will claims personal ownership, distinguishes itself from the innocent, and invites divine judgment on itself alone. This is confession as a full volitional act, not merely a verbal formula. The characteristic thus tests the will at its deepest level: will it own what it has done, or will it use the verbal form while directing the will elsewhere?

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The volitional pattern reveals that conscience suppression *corrupts the will's operating environment*: without the conscience's moral input, the will operates without its designed check. The will remains operative (the person keeps making choices) but its choices are no longer guided by accurate moral information. The corrupted environment progressively reshapes the will's default orientations — the will that has chosen against conscience's witness repeatedly (or chosen to deny it) becomes a will whose default is conscience-absent operation (Tit 3:11 — "warped").

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The volitional pattern reveals that refusal to repent is a *sustained volitional commitment to non-departure*: each moment of "did not depart from" is itself a volitional act (or sustained non-act) that constitutes the characteristic. The cumulative effect of these sustained volitional non-departures is: the will becomes increasingly bound to the sinful course (2Ki 3:3 — "clung to"), the volitional options progressively narrow (Heb 10:26), and the will's default orientation is shaped toward continued refusal. Refusal to repent is thus a self-propagating volitional condition: each act of volitional non-departure makes the next one more likely.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The volitional pattern reveals that habitual defection is the *dispositional form* of the will's sinning capacity: the will has moved from making discrete choices to sin (CHAR-1) through sustained refusal to turn (CHAR-5) into a formed dispositional default toward sin. At the CHAR-6 stage, the will no longer needs to make an active choice to sin — the habitual orientation produces sinning as its natural output. 1Jo 3:6 — "keeps on sinning" — the continuous present describes a volitional state, not a series of discrete decisions. The corrective requires not just a different choice but a reformation of the will's dispositional direction — which is what "abiding in him" (1Jo 3:6) provides.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The volitional pattern reveals that contagious sin respects the community's volitional reality while shaping it: the community members are not forced (their will is not overridden) but their will is gradually shaped through sustained authoritative sinning transmission.
